value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-792740929393008608</id><published>2015-04-30T18:30:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-05-01T10:12:37.277-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1790s"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1803"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1992"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Classical"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Concerto"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Music"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Trumpet"></category><title type="text">Classic Trumpet Concerti of Haydn/Hummel (1992) by Gerard Schwarz, Y Chamber Symphony of New York</title><content type="html">The trumpet has always been a jazz instrument for me. I guess that's in part because I came to jazz before I came to concertos and solo pieces from the classical repertoire and because there really aren't many trumpet pieces out there. It's an under-utilized instrument, for sure. The trumpet always sounds regal or martial to me in Classical and Romantic music and I don't particularly go for that.&lt;br /&gt;Prior to 1770, the trumpet couldn't hit a wide range of notes. The keyed trumpet was invented around then and allowed for the instrument to express a greater range. The result was that composers could actually write music for it! So then we got more interesting trumpet concertos. (The modern trumpet was invented in the 1930s, so very little has been written for this particular type of trumpet.)&lt;br /&gt;Haydn's smacks to me of High Classical conventions or cliches - at least the first movement does - but there is no denying the importance, as it's the first concerto for this type of instrument. So this is basically the first time anyone ever wrote for the trumpet below the high register. And that's kind of crazy. And if I'm being fair, the trumpet really does a lot of stuff in this piece.&lt;br /&gt;The Hummel is apparently one of the few other pieces written for this particular type of trumpet (and was written for the same guy as the Haydn, the inventor of the instrument). I feel like this work is less impressive in terms of the difficulty for the trumpet, but it feels more "modern" to me musically.&lt;br /&gt;Overall this is an excellent pairing of two pieces written for a unique instrument that lost the battle with history.&lt;br /&gt;9/10 </content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/792740929393008608/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=8545641&amp;postID=792740929393008608&amp;isPopup=true" rel="replies" title="0 Comments" type="text/html"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/792740929393008608" rel="edit" type="application/atom+xml"/><link Symphony of New York" type="text/html"/><author><name>Riley Haas</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/102201029100984588753</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image height="32" rel="http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/-n_vvvSADmg0/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAAck/2h5ojO97FxM/s512-c/photo.jpg" width="32"></gd:image></author><thr:total>0</thr:total><gd:extendedproperty name="commentSource" value="1"></gd:extendedproperty><gd:extendedproperty name="commentModerationMode" value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-8865090701191552007</id><published>2015-04-30T18:00:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-05-03T19:32:55.757-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Basketball"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Draft"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="History"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="NBA"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Raptors"></category><title type="text">Raptors Best Draft Picks</title><content type="html">Earlier this season, a click-baity article was &lt;a href="http://www.tsn.ca/raptors-top-five-best-draft-picks-1.216092" target="_blank"&gt;published on TSN&lt;/a&gt; about the "best" Raptors draft picks of all time, given that this was their 20th season and all. They were, according to the author:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ol&gt;&lt;li&gt;Bosh&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Mighty Mouse&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Mo Pete&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;DeRozan&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;T Mac&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ol&gt;No explanation was given for why Mo Pete is considered to be better than DeRozan or T Mac beyond the fact that he played way more games for the Raps. (Does that make him better?) There was also no explanation as to why Mighty Mouse was considered better than T Mac, beyond that the Raptors failed to retain T Mac. That really doesn't make sense. So we're going to try this again.&lt;br /&gt;Special thanks to &lt;a href="https://plus.google.com/+AdamHenebury" target="_blank"&gt;Adam&lt;/a&gt; for helping with the order. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a name='more'&gt;&lt;/a&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;What makes a "best" draft pick? Well, I would argue that it's all about the knowledge the drafting organization had at the time, &lt;i&gt;however&lt;/i&gt;, this is for posterity, and about the players, not about about the organization (this post, anyway) so it's more about:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Is the player going to the Hall of Fame?&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;If not, where does the player stand historically both in the league and, to a lesser extent, in the franchise (if applicable)? &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Finally, how did the player perform compared to the other players in the draft?&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Whether or not that player was retained by the organization seems kind of irrelevant to me, unless we are talking about the organization's decisions, not the players' legacies.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Raptors have drafted 33 players since they were formed 20 years ago. Of those players,&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;7 have never played in the NBA (2 were just drafted this summer, though);&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;2 have played less than 10 NBA games as of today (though 1 of those is Caboclo);&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;2 more have played 20 NBA games or less as of today;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;2 more have played less than 100 NBA games;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;A further 3 have played less than 200 NBA games (though one, Quincy Acy playe a career high minutes for the Knicks this season);&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Finally, both Terrence Ross and JV have yet to play in 250 NBA games and it seems kind of unfair to decide how their careers have panned out given their respective ages. &lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;That leaves us with 15 players who have played 250 games or more in the NBA (i.e 3 seasons minimum). Those players are:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Bargs&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Jonathan Bender&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Bosh&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Camby&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Ed Davis&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;DeMar DeRozan&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Joey Graham&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Hibbert&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Jamison&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;T Mac&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Mo Pete&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Kareem Rush&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Mighty Mouse&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;P.J. Tucker&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Charlie V&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;We should eliminate Terrence Ross from the conversation because he's too young. (Though he has played more than Jonas, he was drafted a year later.) So that leaves us with 15 players, let's rank them!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Note: I have used a totally unscientific method of determining how good these guys were. You have been warned.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;15. Jonathan Bender, SF, drafted 5th overall, 1999&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted immediately after Lamar Odom and drafted immediately ahead of Wally Szczerbiak, Rip Hamilton, Andre Miller, Shawn Marion and Jason Terry. That list doesn't include the other NBA stars who were drafted later.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;1,453P, 582R, 170A in 3,847 minutes over 262 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 13.6P, 5.4R, 1.6A, 0.4S, 1.6P.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.514 True Shooting %age&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;10.9 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year Bender is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;27th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;25th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;29th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;21st in FG% (of players having played at least 200 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in MPG (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in PPG (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;29th in RPG (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in APG (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in Win Shares&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in WS per 48 (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;There's no clearer "bust" on this list than Bender. Yes, his career was cut short by knee injuries, but even when he played he wasn't even close to as good as the players drafted around.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; A month after he was drafted, he was traded &lt;i&gt;straight up&lt;/i&gt; for Antiono Davis. So, talk about a win.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;14. Kareem Rush, SG/PG, drafted 20th overall, 2002&lt;/h4&gt;Rush was drafted a few spots ahead of Tayshaun Prince and John Salmons but this was a pretty weak draft.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;2,213P, 353A, 150S, 572R, 74B in 5,956 minutes over 346 games; 1.7 WS, -3.2 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 13.4P, 2.1A, .9S, 3.5R, .4B&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.482 TS %&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9.2 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&amp;nbsp;In his draft year Rush is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;25th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;22nd in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;29th in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7th in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;24th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;24th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;37th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in Win Shares&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;39th in WS Per 48&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;So Rush mostly almost lived up to his draft position. So he wasn't a bust. Also, his draft kind of sucked. The best players from it were Amar'e (9th), Ming (1st), Boozer (34th!!!) and Caron Butler (10th). So the Raps did good to just get a guy who played relatively close to his draft position. He didn't have much of a career though.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; The day of the draft, he was traded with Tracy Murray and a 2003 2nd rounder to the Lakers for Lindsey Hunter, Chris Jeffries and a 2003 2nd rounder. Meh.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;13. Joey Graham, SF, drafted 16th overall, 2005&lt;/h4&gt;Graham was drafted immediately behind Antoine Wright and, to the eternal chagrin of Raptors fans, immediately ahead of Danny Granger, as well as Gerald Green; he was also drafted ahead of Nate Robinson (21st), Jarret Jack (22nd), David Lee (30th) and some other NBA players.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;2,239P, 1,058R, 207A, 134S, 43B in 6,117 minutes over 377 games; 7.8 WS; -2.8 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 13.2P, 6.2R, 1.2A, .8S, .3B&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.551 TS %&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year Graham is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;30th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;31st in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;30th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;31st in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;34th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;28th in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;34th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;32nd in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;29th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;43rd in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;31st in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;42nd in WS per 48&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;If it's possible to have a bust outside the lottery, I guess Graham was a bust. A second round player drafted ahead of a former all-star (though one who is currently struggling to stay in the league) in the middle of the first round stings a lot.&amp;nbsp; &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; He was allowed to walk as a free agent, which was a very sensible thing for the Raptors to do.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;12. P. J. Tucker, SF/SG, drafted 35th overall, 2006&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted in the second round, which is a total crap shoot. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;2,009P, 1,404R, 375A in 6,866 minutes over 255 games, 14 WS, 5.4 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 10.5P, 7.4R, 2A, 1.5S, 0.3B.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.536 True Shooting %age&amp;nbsp;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12.5 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;br /&gt;In his draft year, Tucker is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;18th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in FG% (of players to play at least 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in 3P FG% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;10th in PPG &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;4th in RPG (ahead of Bargs!)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16th in APG (better than Bargs!)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;15th in Win Shares&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;13th in Win Shares Per 48 (&lt;i&gt;way&lt;/i&gt; higher than Bargs!)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;It's safe to say that Tucker stands as the Best 2nd Round Pick in Raptors History, easily beating out his competition (he has played more NBA games than most of the rest of them combined). But it's fair to ask 'how do we rank that?', as Tucker left the NBA for years and has only amassed these numbers since his return. He absolutely exceeded expectations, but only after he played in Europe and Israel. Is this a better outcome than a player drafted in the first round playing to their draft position???&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;/b&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; He was waived in March 2007.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;11. Charlie Villanueva, PF, drafted 7th overall, 2005&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted immediately behind Martell Webster, immiedately ahead of Channing Frye and a few sports ahead of Andrew Bynum. Also drafted ahead of hte same people as Graham.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;6,489P, 2,096R, 334B, 525A, 311S in 12,913 minutes over 594 games; 22.4 WS; 1 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 18.1P, 8R, .9B, 1.5A, .9S&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.523 TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16.2 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year, Charlie V is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;13th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;18th in minutes&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;21st in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;25th in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;18th in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;22nd in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;33rd in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;19th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in WS (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Not as obviously a pseudo-bust as Graham, but still fairly unsuccessful relative to the other players in his draft. The good news is that, beyond Channing Frye, nobody else immediately below Charlie V's draft spot amounted to much (now that Bynum is out of the league). So it's hard to criticize the pick too much. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; Traded straight up for TJ Ford in June 2006.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;10. Ed Davis, PF/C, drafted 13th overall, 2010&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted a few spots below Paul George, immediately ahead of Patrick Patterson and Larry Sanders and a few spots ahead of Eric Bledsoe and Avery Bradley.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;2,552P, 2,220R, 356B, 284A, 183S in 7,563 minutes over 354 games; 22.1 WS; 5.7 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 12.1P, 10.6R, 1.7B, 1.4A, .9S&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.568 TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16.9 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&amp;nbsp; In his draft year, Davis is&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&amp;nbsp;7th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;13th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;14th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;2nd&lt;/b&gt; in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;27th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;5th&lt;/b&gt; in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in WS per 48&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;So far Davis is having a pretty good career relative to his draft position. His skill set is slowly becoming outmoded in the current NBA (though that could change) but &lt;a href="https://twitter.com/zachlowe_nba/status/489601601162973184" target="_blank"&gt;Zach Lowe thinks he is a more than serviceable NBA player&lt;/a&gt;. Who knows, maybe a better team will eventually use him well. Still sort of sad we got rid of him.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; Traded with Jose Calderon and a 2013 2nd round pick to the Grizzlies while the Pistions traded Austin Daye and Tayshaun Prince to the Grizzlies; in return the Grizzlies traded Calderon to the Pistons and Rudy Gay and Hamed Haddadi to the Raptors. All on January 30, 2013.&amp;nbsp; I know we had to move Jose, but I still don't really like this. &lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;9. Andrea Bargnani, PF/C, drafted 1st overall, 2006&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted  immediately ahead of LMAD, Adam Morrison, Tyrus Thomas, Shelden Williams  and Brandon Roy. Also ahead of Gay (8th), JJ Redick (10th), Rondo  (21st), Lowry (24th), Paul Millsap (47th) and, of course, PJ Tucker.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;7,569P, 2,444R, 461B, 635A, 203S in 15,172 minutes over 504 games; 18.7 WS; .1 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 18P, 5.8R, 1.1B, 1.5A, .5S&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.532 TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;14.5 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year, Bargnani is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;5th&lt;/b&gt; in boards (behind Rondo!!!)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;14th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;20th in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7th 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;5th&lt;/b&gt; in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;5th&lt;/b&gt; in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;19th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;32nd in WS per 48 (27th if we cut it off at 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Of all the 7 footers to play 500 games or more in the NBA (62 of them), Bargs is somehow 53rd in RPG. That is incredible. And says everything you need to know about him.&lt;br /&gt;So,  I'm sure you're wondering why I don't think he was a bust. Why I could  suggest that only Bender and, perhaps, Graham, were busts. Well, for a  couple of reasons.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Despite are hatred of Bargs, he still  managed to be a top 5 player in his draft year in terms of many  categories and I don't think you can call that a bust - the draft sucked  donkey balls;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Look at &lt;a href="http://www.basketball-reference.com/draft/NBA_2006.html" target="_blank"&gt;who came immediately after him&lt;/a&gt;: LMAD was the only other player still in the league among the top 6 until Tyrus Thomas made a come back this season;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;In  hindsight LMAD was the right choice and Roy would have been an  excellent choice too, despite his injury problems (if only becuse he was  still way better than the 3 players between him and LMAD);&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;I  think, relatively speaking, Morrison is a worse pick, as was Thomas  (maybe not Williams given where he went) - Bargs would have been a  pretty solid pick at 3 or 4 and you shouldn't be able to say that about  busts;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Also, lots of people thought he was the next Dirk (though far from everyone).&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;So  yeah, Bargs sucks. Good riddance. So glad the Knicks are the Knicks.  But I really think his status as bust has been exagerrated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; (Or, rather, how did we get free of him?) Traded to the Knicks for Marcus Camby (bought out), Steve Novak, Quentin Richardson (waived), a 2014 2nd rounder, a 2016 1st rounder and a 2017 2nd rounder in one of the greatest transactions in recent franchise history, on July 10, 2013. That was a happy, happy day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;8. Morris Peterson, SF/SG, drafted 21st overall, 2000&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted immiedately after Speedy Claxton and two spots ahead of DeShawn Stevenson.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;7,628P, 2,483R, 1,090A, 639S, 136B in 19,366 minutes over 711 games; 35.7 WS; 9.7 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 14.2P, 4.6R, 2A, 1.2S, .3B&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.529 TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;13.3 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year, Mo Pete is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;8th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;8th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;10th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;23rd in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;5th in 3P% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;19th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;18th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in Win Shares&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;12th in WS per 48 (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Mo Pete is the all-time leader in games played for the franchise and he's certainly beloved, but in no way does that make him the third best draft pick in Raptors history. What a claim like that says is that it matters whether or not (or when) the player is traded, which has nothing to do with the player, most of the time. So I find that kind of reasoning confusing (in addition to being wrong).&lt;br /&gt;Sure he did extremely well compared to his draft position, but &lt;a href="http://www.basketball-reference.com/draft/NBA_2000.html" target="_blank"&gt;it was a terrible draft&lt;/a&gt;; the best players were Michael Redd, &lt;i&gt;Hedo Turkoglu&lt;/i&gt;, Mike Miller and Kenyon Martin. It was &lt;a href="http://insider.espn.go.com/nba/insider/story/_/id/10714672/nba-2013-14-rookie-class-worst-ever" target="_blank"&gt;probably the worst draft in history&lt;/a&gt;. So it's amazing the Raps got an NBA player, let alone one who eventually played over 700 games. But that doesn't make Mo Pete the third greatest draft pick in Raptors history. It just means he did way better than he should of (as did the team), all other things being equal.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; Allowed to walk as a free agent.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;7. Roy Hibbert, C, drafted 17th overall, 2008&lt;/h4&gt;Drafted immediately  after Marreese Speights, immediately ahead of Javale McGee and JJ  Hickson, and a few spots ahead of Ryan Anderson. Also drafted ahead of  Serge Ibaka, George Hill, Nikola Pekovic, Omer Asik and Goran Dragic.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;5,909P, 3,623R, 990B, 769A, 201S in 13,829 minutes over 533 games; 31.9 WS; 8.6 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 15.4P, 9.4R, 2.6B, 2A, .5S&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.511 TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16.2 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;2 All Star Game appearances&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;1 All Defensive 2nd Team &lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year, Hibbert is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;2nd&lt;/b&gt; in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;8th in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;8th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;13th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in FG% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;25th in 3P% (min 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;24th in FT% (ditto)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;16th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;15th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;17th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;10th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;18th in WS per 48&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Not too long ago, Hibbert might have placed above DeRozan on  this list. How things have changed. He was still an excellent choice in  his spot as Ibaka was drated 7 places below him and it seems  unreasonable to me to think the Raps would have dreamed of taking him  that high.&lt;br /&gt;It's a shame the Raps traded him away immediately, in a trade that will live in infamy:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;To the Pacers: Maceo Baston, TJ Ford, Hibbert &lt;i&gt;and&lt;/i&gt; Rasho&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;To the Raps: Nathan "The Australian Shaq" Jawai and Jermaine O'Neal&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;b&gt;How did he get away?&lt;/b&gt; See the above disaster, about two weeks after the draft.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;6. DeMar DeRozan, SG, drafted 9th overall, 2009&lt;/h4&gt;DeRozan was drafted immiedately behind Jordan Hill (YES!!!), immediately ahead of Brandon Jennings, and a few spots ahead of Gerald Henderson and Tyler Hansbrough.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;7,606P, 1,056A, 411S, 1,689R, 129B in 14,851 minutes over 443 games; 25.5 WS; 1.2 VORP&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 18.4P, 2.6A, 1S, 4.1R, .3B&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;.524 TS% &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;15.3 PER&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;1 All Star Game appearance &lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;In his draft year, DeRozan is:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;2nd&lt;/b&gt; in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;u&gt;&lt;i&gt;&lt;b&gt;1st&lt;/b&gt;&lt;/i&gt;&lt;/u&gt; in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;20th in FG% (minimum 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;35th in 3P% (ditto) &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in FT% (minimum 100 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;&lt;b&gt;4th&lt;/b&gt; in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;14th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;15th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;26th in WS per 48&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;It's hard to know where DeRozan will end up on this overall list until he plays a lot more games but so far he appears to have been a really, really good choice at the 9th spot. He still struggles with his efficiency and he lacks an outside shot, but otherwise I think Raptors fans have to remain happy with the choice that was made (for once!); it's not DeRozan's fault that the Raps have failed to acquire a bigger star.&lt;br /&gt;So really his spot on this list is TBD.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.ca/2015/05/the-top-5-raptors-draft-picks-of-all.html" target="_blank"&gt;See the Top 5&lt;/a&gt;</content><link value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-2951301801353642623</id><published>2015-04-30T17:30:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-04-30T17:30:01.605-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2015"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Documentary"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Hot Docs"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Palestine"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Racing"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Women"></category><title type="text">Speed Sisters (2015, Amber Fares)</title><content type="html">This is an entertaining and captivating documentary about the Palestinian women's car racing team, who supply their own cars, who race against men (and each other) and who practice in empty parkling lots and on local streets. Racing in Palestine is (I believe) unlike anything else in the world, as the races have to be designed for the circumstances, so it's all about turning around cones and going the correct direction (without signs to tell you which way that is, so the driver has to memorize the route) on an open paved area. The film catpures what is like to be a female race car driver in an Arab-Islamic society, and one that also happens to be occupied by Israel. There's a lot going on here, and it's a testament to the filmmaker (this is her first feature!!!) that she is able to balance everything most of the time.&lt;br /&gt;The film has some pacing issues and doesn't even get to the race that it initially sets us up for (and I have no idea why) but otherwise, this is a great insight into life in another culture and country, a side of Palestine we never see on the news, and a film that manages to make you feel good about people and where we're at in the world.&lt;br /&gt;8/10</content><link scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Short Film"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Sports"></category><title type="text">Hell Runs on Gasoline (2015, Martin Bureau)</title><content type="html">This is an extraordinary 7 minute film about something I was utterly unaware of: the absolutely insane, free-for-all racing in &lt;a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Saint-F%C3%A9licien,_Quebec" target="_blank"&gt;Saint-Felicien, Quebec&lt;/a&gt;. I cannot begin to describe how nuts this race is, or how well this short captures the chaos. Basically, I practically wanted to go for one of these races by the time the film was over. Really cool.&lt;br /&gt;9/10</content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/2999448213164469122/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link type="text/html"/><author><name>Riley Haas</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/102201029100984588753</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image height="32" rel="http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/-n_vvvSADmg0/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAAck/2h5ojO97FxM/s512-c/photo.jpg" value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-6646582436916987553</id><published>2015-04-29T18:00:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-04-29T18:00:01.630-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1770s"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Classical"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Music"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Piano music"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Sonata"></category><title type="text">Franz Joseph Haydn: Keyboard Works 1773-1779 (1995) by Lola Odiaga</title><content type="html">This is a collection of six of Haydn's keyboard sonatas (played on piano) ostensibly written between 1883 and 1779. (However, there appears to be some debate.) The sonatas are Nos. 39, 40, 41, 48, 49 and 51, which seems an arbitrary selection. However, the alernative cataloguing of Haydn's works (really, the standard catalogue) suggests that all but 49 were composed during two particular moments, so maybe that's why. (Okay, I'll stop.)&lt;br /&gt;The 39th is a gorgeous piece of music. Very, very Classical, but still interesting enough (and clearly difficult) that it isn't just a simple melody.&lt;br /&gt;The 40th is really whacky and out there, for it's time anyway. I love this kind of thing where it skirts along, threatening to break rules but never quite breaking them. In the showy parts you almost, &lt;i&gt;almost&lt;/i&gt; lose the melody. Really great.&lt;br /&gt;The 41st starts off sounding really traditional but there are still lots of moments for the player to show off.&amp;nbsp;&amp;nbsp; This one is pretty playful actually. I like it.&lt;br /&gt;The 48th is very jaunty in the style you would really associate with this era. However, again Haydn shows that he's not just any old composer. He varies the left hand from phrase to phrase, and that's before the piece really takes off about a minute in. Good stuff.&lt;br /&gt;The 49th is rather dark compared to the others in this collection, but that's because of the key, obviously. It's still not Romantic dark, but it's borderline (which reminds me of a number of his late symphonies). It might be my least favourite of the group, though. Just a little too straightforward.&lt;br /&gt;The 51st appears to be the most famous here as it is the only one with a wikpedia entry. It constantly shifts tempos and seems to jump all over the place.&amp;nbsp; Though a couple parts are hummable most of it shows off the player's ability. You often think it's about to head to cliche/convention, but then it does not. I can see why it's famous.&lt;br /&gt;I guess the collection is a little bit arbitrary but it's tough to curate these down to a single disc anyway, as there are 60 ish of these. The music that is here is fantastic and once again Haydn forces me to rethink Classical.&lt;br /&gt;9/10 </content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/6646582436916987553/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=8545641&amp;postID=6646582436916987553&amp;isPopup=true" rel="replies" title="0 Comments" type="text/html"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/6646582436916987553" rel="edit" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/6646582436916987553" rel="self" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/2015/04/franz-joseph-haydn-keyboard-works-1773.html" rel="alternate" title="Franz Joseph Haydn: Keyboard Works 1773-1779 (1995) by Lola Odiaga" type="text/html"/><author><name>Riley Haas</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/102201029100984588753</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image height="32" rel="http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/-n_vvvSADmg0/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAAck/2h5ojO97FxM/s512-c/photo.jpg" width="32"></gd:image></author><thr:total>0</thr:total><gd:extendedproperty name="commentSource" value="1"></gd:extendedproperty><gd:extendedproperty name="commentModerationMode" value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-5227994287246960008</id><published>2015-04-29T17:00:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-04-29T17:00:02.738-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2014"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2015"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Basketball"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="NBA"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Raptors"></category><title type="text">Your 2014-15 Toronto Raptors</title><content type="html">Last year, as the Raptors neared setting a record for regular season wins in a season, I wondered &lt;a href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.ca/2014/04/best-raptors-team-ever.html" target="_blank"&gt;which was the best Raptors team ever&lt;/a&gt;. A weeks later &lt;a href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.ca/2014/05/your-2013-14-toronto-raptors.html" target="_blank"&gt;I concluded last year's edition ranked among the best&lt;/a&gt;. But at the beginning of this calendar year, &lt;a href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.ca/2015/01/2014-was-year-of-raptor.html" target="_blank"&gt;I was optimistic that we were seeing the best team in the history of the franchise&lt;/a&gt;. And now that team has been swept in the most embarassing way imaginable, with the final game looking like a no-contest.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;a name='more'&gt;&lt;/a&gt;This team still set the record for most wins in a regular season (49), highest winning percentage in the regular season (.598) and won the team's third division title (an utterly meaningless thing, especially in the Altantic). However, this is a team that was winning nearly 80% of its games in the fall and was on pace for 60 wins at one point. Yeah, we should have expected a regression, but this bad a regression? The Raptors were 15-5 in their first 20 games. As of Christmas day they were 22-7. &lt;b&gt;22-7!!!&lt;/b&gt; They finished the regular season 49-33 and the finished with a 49-47 overall record thanks to The Sweep. That's a massive, massive swing in the wrong direction. (Last year's team managed 51-38 if you include the playoffs.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Now I know there was no plan for a Lowry-DeRozan playoff team post Rudy Gay. I understand that this was a ll a lucky fluke, that the Raps were back to making the playoffs when they were supposed to be tearing it down. But that doesn't make this sting less. So, for a record setting year, this will be a rather sad summary, I guess.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(As usual, players are ranked by minutes played. Ages are as of February 1, 2015.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Kyle Lowry, 28, PG:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;34.5 MPG; Per 36: 18.6P, 7.1A, 1.6S, 4.9R, .2B; 19.3 PER; .527 TS% in 70 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 15.2P, 6.8A, 1.6S, 4.8R, .3B; 17.3 Career PER; .546 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;$12 mil per season until 2017 with a player option for 2018&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Acquired by Bryan Colangelo for Gary Forbes and a 2013 first round pick (Steven Adams)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Lowry got off to a hot start and got his all-star game appearance that many people though he deserved the season prior, and he carried the team when DeRozan went down. Unfortunately Lowry was clearly warn out by the end of the season and possibly injured. Also, lacking his co-star, he started playing a lot more selfishly. Those two things resulted in this ugly performance during The Sweep:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;32.8 MPG;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 13.5, 5.2A, 1.4S, 5.5R, 0B with 4.5 fouls and 3 Turnovers&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;7.9 PER; .396 TS%; -.3 WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Lowry will be "basketball old" by the end of his current contract and it's worth thinking about a post-Lowry Raptors team for that very reason and also because it seems pretty obvious that the Raptors cannot even be an okay playoff team with Lowry as their best or 2nd best player. I love Lowry, but it's probably for the best that this team got killed. Had they killed the Wizards and given a second round opponent some grief, we might have all been thinking we had something.&lt;br /&gt;(Please note, however, that if this becomes a Casey vs. Lowry decision - based on some rumours I am hearing this week - I am firmly on Lowry's side at the moment. I was not impressed by Casey during The Sweep. Not at all.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Patrick Patterson, 25, PF:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;26.6 MPG; Per 36: 10.8P, 7.2R, .7B, 2.6A, 1S; 14.6 PER; .568 TS% in 81 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 12.7P, 7.4R, .9B, 1.9A, .9S; 14.4 Career PER; .538 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;About $6 per season until 2017&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Acquired by Masai Ujiri with Chuck Hayes, John Salmons, and Greivis Vasquez for Rudy Gay, Quincy Acy and Aaron Gray on December 9, 2013&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;It's a miracle that a team with Patterson as it's second most important player won 49 games. That's not meant to be a slight on 2Pat. It's more meant to raise awareness about how this team was hampered by injuries and, perhaps, by bizarre lineups. 2Pat is the Raps' stretch 4 and that's a common thing these days, but there's no way he's the team's second best player, as was reflected in the playoffs, when the team was healthier and Patterson tied for 6th in total minutes. Patterson scored as much as could be expected during The Sweep, but got beaten up on the boards by the Wiz.&lt;br /&gt;2Pat is a fine complimentary player but that's all. Likely a 7th man or perhaps even farther down the depth chart on a good team.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;DeMar DeRozan, 25, SG:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;35 MPG; Per 36: 20.6P, 3.6A, 1.3S, 4.7R, .2B; 17.4 PER; .510 TS% in 60 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 18.4P, 2.6A, 1S, 4.1R, .3B; 15.3 Career PER; .524 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;$9.5 mil per season until 2016 with a player option for 2017&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Drafted by Bryan Colangelo 9th overall in 2009&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;DeRozan's year was obviously deeply affected by his injury and he saw a bit of dip in his scoring as well as a significant dip in his efficiency. And like Lowry, he didn't have a good playoff (though it was hardly as bad as Lowry's). Given his age, his salary and his skill level, DeRozan is a much better bet to stick around past any rejigging of the team than Lowry, but I personally don't ever see DeRozan being more than the 2nd or 3rd option on a great team. And I have no idea how that would ever happen. But I guess he remains the future until we can find something better.&lt;br /&gt;Just as an aside: DeRozan has turned out rather well compared to the rest of his draft class. He is&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;2nd in games played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;1st in minutes played&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;4th in points&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in boards&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;11th in assists&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in FG% (minimum 400 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;6th in FT% (minimum 400 games)&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;4th in MPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;4th in PPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;14th in RPG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;15th in APG&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;9th in WS&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;And remember, he was drafted 9th. So we did well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Jonas Valanciunas, 22, C:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;26.2 MPG; Per 36: 16.5P, 11.9R, 1.6B, .7A, .6S; 20.6 PER; .623 TS% in 80 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 14.9P, 10.9R, 1.5B, .9A, .5S, 17.6 Career PER;&amp;nbsp; .605 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Rookie deal until 2016&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Drafted by Bryan Colangelo 5th overall in 2011&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Despite getting played a lot less, JV had a career year offensively, in terms of both overall and efficiency. And certainly Casey's handling of him has to be one of the main reasons (in addition to The Sweep) that Ujiri has to think seriously about either getting rid of Casey or trying to move JV for something else. Casey seems terrified to use him late in the game and that's frustrating because JV is still only 22 and big man defence takes a long time to learn in the NBA. Offensively, he's getting close to where I think a lot of people were hoping he'd be, when Casey lets him play. I know this team was trying to win games, but it would be nice if they could also try to develop their supposed centre of the future.&lt;br /&gt;So there's a big choice coming up. Are they patient and hope that eventually learns NBA defence or do they try to move him for someone more polished ?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Terrence Ross, 23, SF/SG:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;25.5 MPG; Per 36: 13.9P, 3.9R, 1.5A, .9S, .4B; 11.2 PER; .519 TS% in 82 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 14.1P, 4.1R, 1.4A, 1S, .4B; 11.3 Career PER; .526 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Rookie Deal ending in 2016&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Drafted by Bryan Colangelo 8th overall in 2012&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Ross had his sophomore slump in his third season, seeing a regression both in his scoring and his efficiency. He also appeared (to me) to be more inconsistent on defence. 3 years in, Ross isn't a bust but a lot of us wondered why he started 61 games when there was a better bigger player capable of playing his position. And his inability to excel consistently at the either end suggests the idea that if there is another team out there who looks at him and sees potential maybe he should be moved. It's hard to see him as a major piece going forward anyway.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Lou Williams, 28, SG/PG:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;25.2 MPG; Per 36: 22.2P, 2.9A, 1.6S, 2.7R, .2B; 19.9 PER; .564 TS% in 80 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 18.8P, 4.6A, 1.4S, 3.1R, .3B; 17.5 Career PER; .540 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;UFA&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Acquired by Masai Ujiri with Lucas Nogueira for the corpse of John Salmons&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Williams won the 6th Man of the Year award for his career (by PP36) or near-career (by PER) year this season. However the "Give Lou the ball to bail us out" strategy failed utterly in the playoffs when his True Shooting %age dropped &lt;i&gt;130 points&lt;/i&gt;. Williams is one of those players who is great when he's hitting and not of much use when he's not (though he was better defensively than I was expecting). Williams is probably getting paid because of his award and I for one don't think the Raptors should be the team to pay him, if only because we know what he is and 6th Man of the Year will probably be his career peak. Can Ujiri sign him for the hometown discount and trade him to someone who needs bench offense?&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Greivis Vasquez, 29, PG:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;24.3 MPG; Per 36: 14P, 5.5A, .8S, 3.9R, .2B; 12.6 PER; .514 TS% in 82 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 13.8P, 7.3A, .9S, 3.9R, .1B; 14 Career PER; .513 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;$6.6 mil until 2016&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Acquired by Masai Ujiri with Chuck Hayes, Patrick Patterson and John Salmons for Quincy Acy, Rudy Gay and Aaron Gray&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Last year the Lowry-Vasquez double point guard lineup killed the Eastern Conference. For some reason it didn't work as well this year. For one thing Vasquez saw his shooting percentages drop back down towards his career numbers. Also, Vasquez is too slow to guard his position a lot of the time, but we knew that already. Otherwise, I don't really know what happened -&amp;nbsp; maybe it was the arrival of Lou Williams. Anyway his regular season was only marginally worse than last year; it was the playoffs where he really struggled (with the exception of a few huge shots early in the series).&lt;br /&gt;Vasquez is one of the oldest players on the team. It's unlikely he's part of the long-term.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Amir Johnson, 27, PF/C:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;26.4 MPG; Per 36: 12.6P, 8.3R, 1.1B, 2.1A, .8S; 15.4 PER; .603 TS% in 75 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 12.2P, 9.1R, 1.7B, 1.7A, 1S; 16.1 Career PER; .603 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;UFA&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Acquired by Bryan Colangelo with Sonny Weems for Carlos Delfino and Roko Ukic&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Amir remains the Raptors' best interior defender but he's struggling with injuries and though he's fouling less, he still fouls an awful lot. Unlike the rest of the team he actually did alright in the playoffs.&lt;br /&gt;I have no idea what to do here. I figured Amir is going to have more and more ankle issues as he ages. On the other hand, without him, the Raps are really, really weak when it comes to defensive bigs.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;James Johnson, 27, SF/PF:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 14.6P, 6.8R, 2.5A, 1.4S, 1.8B; 17.9 PER; .617 TS% in 70 minutes&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 13.1P, 6.4R, 3A, 1.5S, 1.9B; 14.5 Career PER; .528 Career TS% &lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;$2.5 mil until 2016&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Signed by Masai Ujiri on July 15, 2014&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;Despite having one of the best years of his career, Johnson inexplicably started 17 games to Ross' 61. Now, it's not the starts that matter, it's the finishes. Casey played Ross for over 700 minutes more. Was this some attempt to see what they had in Ross? To let him grow up? I don't know. Johnson is a much more mature player than he was the first time around in Toronto. Yes, he still makes boneheaded decisions on offence, but he is the team's best wing defender. And he doesn't make as many boneheaded decisions as he used to. He played a total of 12 minutes during The Sweep and I have no idea why. No idea.(I know he missed four consecutive free throws, but the Raptors basically didn't play defense and he would have helped that.)&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;h4&gt;Tyler Hansbrough, 29, PF:&lt;/h4&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Per 36: 9.2P, 9R, .5B, .7A, 1.S; 13.3 PER; .597 TS% in 74 games&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Career Per 36: 14.5P, 9R, .4B, .9A, 1S; 14.9 Career PER; .525 Career TS%&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;UFA&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Signed by Masai Ujiri on July 15, 2013&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;I would be surprised if Hansbrough is retained this summer. He's done a decent job of fulfilling his role on the Raps but players of his skill set are slowly becoming less and less useful in the modern NBA, I think. (Though there're always reasons to buck a trend.) If he does come back, he'd likely be cheap.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That's everone who played 1000 minutes in the regular season this year. Hell, that's everyone who played 500 minutes. &lt;i&gt;300&lt;/i&gt; minutes. The Raps had a deep bench up to a point. Of the remaining players:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;ul&gt;&lt;li&gt;Chuck Hayes is an UFA and the oldest player on the team - he will not be back;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;The organization is finally out from under the terrible Landry Fields contract this summer - I will be amazed if he isn't playing in Europe or China next season;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;Gret Stiemsa was a warm body on the veteran's minimum - another may take his place;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;I have no idea what to think about Lucas Nogueira but at least we got him for free practically;&lt;/li&gt;&lt;li&gt;I remain very skeptical about Bruno Caboclo but I also know zero about basketball player development - if this was hockey I would be demanding he start every game in the D League.&lt;/li&gt;&lt;/ul&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The Raptors are at a crossroads: is losing in a game 7 in the first round the peak potential of a Lowry-DeRozan core? I didn't feel that way three weeks ago. I sure do now. (Let me be clear: I didn't think the Raps would make it past the second round, but I at least hoped they would win some games and maybe make it &lt;i&gt;to&lt;/i&gt; the second round.)&lt;br /&gt;I for one support a change of direction at this point. I am okay with moving on from this group. Unless, with the new cap situation in a year or so, the Raps can attract or acquire a player or two clearly better than DeRozan (and who plays a complimentary position, as opposed to who plays essentially the same game as him cough Rudy Gay cough) then I think it's okay to stick with these guys for a few more years. But if Lowry and DeRozan remain the best players on this team, I think first round exits are our future until 2018, and I don't look forward to that. So I am perfectly comfortable with the idea that no one on this roster is untouchable. So hopefully things improve. I still have some faith in Ujiri at this point, especially given that he didn't make a move at the trade deadilne. So I am optimistic.&lt;br /&gt;And now I will go back to crying myself to sleep. Sob.</content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/5227994287246960008/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-7359870065971575822</id><published>2015-04-28T17:30:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-04-28T17:30:01.266-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1760s"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="1780s"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2003"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2010"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Cello"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Classical"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Concerto"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Music"></category><title type="text">Haydn: Cello Concertos; Pereira: Concertino for Cello (2010) by Antonio Meneses, Northern Sinfonia</title><content type="html">This is an odd collection that pairs Haydn's two most famous (and likely sole surviving) cello concerti with a totally unrelated piece of music by the 20th century composer Clovis Pereira. Grumble.&lt;br /&gt;Haydn's first cello concerto is a fine piece of music but it strikes me as typical of the era (though I don't really know that). Though the cello is perhaps my favourite orchestral instrument I can't help but compare this work to what came before - specially Bach's cello music, which is probably the best ever written (or at least very close to that). This is fine, really, and it certainly has a number of beautiful passages for the instrument, but it's a little too classically Classical (see what I did there?) for me. This is apparently the first cello concerto ever. So I should really just get over myself.&lt;br /&gt;The Pereira "Concertino" is very pleasant albeit traditional. The composer apparently tried to combine some tradtional Brazilian folk melodies with at least some baroque influences that the Portuguese would have brought to Brazil when they were colonizing it. I don't know enough about Brazillian music to know if the folk part is true, but this is certainly a Neo Baroque attitude, not Baroque. (To be fair, he calls it "Quasi Baroque" which still seems to me quite a stretch.) The second movement is gorgeous. The third reminds me of a melody from a film soundtrack. I have no idea why it's included here.&lt;br /&gt;The second cello concerto was once thought to be the only surviving one. (At one point, &lt;i&gt;five&lt;/i&gt; cello concerti were attributed to Haydn; it's down to three and one is lost.) This is a lot more laidback than the first, which gives it an entirely different aura than the earlier work. It is, at times, significantly different in tone than I would have expected from a work of its era. So, at least initially, I like it more. For example, the first movement has a pretty crazy solo passage.&lt;br /&gt;It's an odd collection; the Haydn music is pretty essential but it's so odd that they couldn't find something more appropriate to pair with it than a moder work composed in the 21st century. An odd choice.&lt;br /&gt;7/10</content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/7359870065971575822/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=8545641&amp;postID=7359870065971575822&amp;isPopup=true" rel="replies" title="0 Comments" type="text/html"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/7359870065971575822" rel="edit" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/7359870065971575822" rel="self" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/2015/04/haydn-cello-concertos-pereira.html" rel="alternate" title="Haydn: Cello Concertos; Pereira: Concertino for Cello (2010) by Antonio Meneses, Northern Sinfonia" type="text/html"/><author><name>Riley Haas</name><uri>https://plus.google.com/102201029100984588753</uri><email>noreply@blogger.com</email><gd:image height="32" rel="http://schemas.google.com/g/2005#thumbnail" src="//lh3.googleusercontent.com/-n_vvvSADmg0/AAAAAAAAAAI/AAAAAAAAAck/2h5ojO97FxM/s512-c/photo.jpg" width="32"></gd:image></author><thr:total>0</thr:total><gd:extendedproperty name="commentSource" value="1"></gd:extendedproperty><gd:extendedproperty name="commentModerationMode" value="FILTERED_POSTMOD"></gd:extendedproperty></entry><entry><id>tag:blogger.com,1999:blog-8545641.post-5025626102013630858</id><published>2015-04-28T17:00:00.000-04:00</published><updated>2015-04-28T17:00:01.648-04:00</updated><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="2014"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Documentary"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Foreign Policy"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Hot Docs"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Intelligence Failures"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Iraq War"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="Movies"></category><category scheme="http://www.blogger.com/atom/ns#" term="War"></category><title type="text">War of Lies (2014, Mathias Bittner)</title><content type="html">Let's get this out of the way: This is a student film. The director freely admitted last night that he made this as his graduation "project" for film school.&amp;nbsp; When he said that &lt;i&gt;before&lt;/i&gt; the movie, my expectations lowered considerably. I am always wary of first time directors.&lt;br /&gt;And there are definitely signs that this is a first freature: too much use of the static between TV clips, which is such a cliche; awkward pacing; unnecessary scenes; etc.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;i&gt;But&lt;/i&gt;...and it's a big 'but': This is one compelling film. Here we have an interview with one of the couple major sources for the US's bogus intelligence for the 2003 invasion of Iraq. This is the guy who claimed that there were mobile chemical weapons factories. This interview is about why he said what he said and how he feels about it now. The film is just the interview, plus Bittner's attempts at drametizing Aljanabi's state of mind - I worried those attempts would be awkard but, for the most part, they work really well as a means of placing the viewer inside his mental state (provided, of course, Aljanabi is telling the truth, and we have no reason to believe he is). I don't think I have ever seen a film like this - one subject telling his side of a story with the film set out to show how he felt. It's like one of those TV shows about near-death experiences but with only one interviewee, no narrators, and it's way, way better.&lt;br /&gt;Regardless of whether or not Aljanabi is telling the truth, the film is a damning indictment of both the German Federal Intelligence Service and the CIA, and anyone else who believed this nonsense (MI6 for example). It's a perfect example of how human beings hear what they want to hear. At this point hundreds of thousands (I recently heard "one million or more") people died in part because the Federal Intelligence Service decided Aljanabi was credible. If that doesn't make you angry, nothing will.&lt;br /&gt;An absolute must see despite the odd technical issue.&lt;br /&gt;9/10</content><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/feeds/5025626102013630858/comments/default" rel="replies" title="Post Comments" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/comment.g?blogID=8545641&amp;postID=5025626102013630858&amp;isPopup=true" rel="replies" title="0 Comments" type="text/html"/><link href="http://www.blogger.com/feeds/8545641/posts/default/5025626102013630858" rel="edit" type="application/atom+xml"/><link href="http://superchicken46.blogspot.com/2015/04/war-of-lies-2014-mathias-bittner.html" rel="alternate" title="War of Lies (2014, Mathias Bittner)" type="text/html"/><author><name>Riley
